# Warhammer 40k - 8th Edition Concept Map - Concept Map

Concept map generated from: Warhammer 40k - 8th Edition

**Total Concepts (Nodes):** 1338
**Total Relations (Edges):** 1537

---

## Concepts

### Level 0 - Foundational

#### Fortified Stronghold Stratagem

A Defender stratagem used before Firestorm Attacks to increase one Bastion's wounds from 20 to 25.

**Tags:** stratagem, defender, bastions

**Related:** Firestorm Attack

---

#### Targeting Jammers Stratagem

A Defender stratagem used before Firestorm Attacks to move one Firestorm location dice up to 2D6 inches in any direction.

**Tags:** stratagem, defender, Firestorm Attack

**Related:** Firestorm Attack Dice Placement

---

#### Rapid Drop Assault Stratagem

An Attacker stratagem used before Reserve rolls at the start of the first turn that causes D3 units to automatically arrive from Reserve.

**Tags:** stratagem, attacker, reserve arrival

**Related:** Tactical Priority

---

#### Scorched Skies Stratagem

An Attacker stratagem used before Firestorm Attacks that allows making D3 additional Firestorm Attacks.

**Tags:** stratagem, attacker, Firestorm Attack

**Related:** Firestorm Attack

---

#### Infantry Units Going to Ground

An option for infantry units during Firestorm attacks where they suffer reduced mortal wounds (D3) but cannot act in their first turn.

**Also known as:** Infantry Going to Ground

**Tags:** damage mitigation, unit status, Planetstrike

**Related:** Firestorm Attack

---

#### Transport (Deployment)

A vehicle or unit used to carry other units, where embarked units arrive on the battlefield together with the transport during deployment from Reserve.

**Tags:** deployment, unit transport, game mechanic

**Related:** Transport, Deployment

---

#### Icarus Lascannon

A heavy weapon with a 96" range, 1 shot, Strength 9, AP -3, and 1 damage often mounted on Defence Emplacements.

**Tags:** weapon profile, heavy weapon, ranged weapon

**Related:** Defence Emplacements

---

#### Quad-Gun

A heavy weapon with a 48" range, 8 shots, Strength 7, AP -1, and 1 damage used in Defence Emplacements.

**Tags:** weapon profile, heavy weapon, ranged weapon

**Related:** Defence Emplacements

---

#### Heavy Bolter

A heavy weapon with a 36" range, 3 shots, Strength 5, AP -1, and damage D6 used in fortifications like Bastions.

**Tags:** weapon profile, heavy weapon, ranged weapon

**Related:** Bastions

---

#### Defence Emplacements

Immobile defensive weapons with Toughness 7, Save 4+, 3 wounds, armed with an Icarus lascannon or quad-gun, which automatically get hit in fights and have modifiers when shooting flying units or those arriving from orbit.

**Also known as:** Defence Emplacements

**Tags:** defensive position, weapon system, planetary assault

**Related:** Quad-Gun, Icarus Lascannon, Defender (Planetstrike Role)

---

#### Bastions

Immovable defensive structures with Toughness 10, Save 3+, 20 wounds, and four heavy bolters, that shelter Defender units during invasions and automatically get hit in fights without hit rolls.

**Also known as:** Planetstrike Bastions

**Tags:** defensive structure, planetary assault, fortification

**Related:** Garrisoning Bastions, Heavy Bolter, Defender (Planetstrike Role)

---

#### Landing Zone

A designated area off one battlefield edge where non-orbiting units in Reserve deploy within 6 inches of that edge when arriving from Reserve.

**Tags:** deployment, battlefield, planetary assault, battlefield positioning

**Related:** Reserve Units, Deployment

---

#### Reserve Units

Units that start the game off the battlefield and arrive later by rolling a dice each movement phase, with infantry and FLY units starting in orbit and others in a landing zone.

**Also known as:** Reserves

**Tags:** deployment, unit status, planetary assault, game mechanics, units

**Related:** Landing Zone, Deployment, Astropath, Astronomican

---

#### Firestorm Attack

An attack initiated by the Attacker at the start of the first battle round, placing six dice numbered 1 to 6 at least 9” apart, with units within 3” of rolled locations suffering D6 mortal wounds.

**Also known as:** Initial Firestorm Attack

**Tags:** attack phase, damage effect, planetary assault, combat mechanics, game phase

**Related:** Infantry Units Going to Ground, Scorched Skies Stratagem, Fortified Stronghold Stratagem

---

#### Defender (Planetstrike Role)

The player role in Planetstrike charged with holding strong fortifications against invasion and repelling attacking forces.

**Also known as:** Planetstrike Defender

**Tags:** player role, objective, planetary defense

**Related:** Planetstrike, Defence Emplacements, Bastions

---

#### Attacker (Planetstrike Role)

The player role in Planetstrike who tries to seize control of the planet by launching firestorms and deploying troops to capture strongholds.

**Also known as:** Planetstrike Attacker

**Tags:** player role, objective, planetary assault

**Related:** Planetstrike

---

#### Planetstrike

An expansion for planetary assault games featuring two players as Attacker and Defender, where players fight for control of a planet amid intense battlefield conditions.

**Also known as:** Planetary Assault Expansion

**Tags:** game mode, planetary assault, expansion, battlefield setup, planetary invasion, Warhammer 40k

**Related:** Attacker (Planetstrike Role), Defender (Planetstrike Role)

---

#### Orbital Bombardment Stratagem

A special stratagem that modifies Meteoric Debris rules to place six dice instead of three, enhances psyker abilities by adding to Psychic and Deny the Witch tests, doubles psychic power ranges, and causes special Terrors of the Warp when doubles are rolled.

**Also known as:** Orbital Bombardment

**Tags:** stratagem, psychic enhancement, shooting phase, warp

**Related:** Meteoric Debris, State of the Imperium

---

#### Perils of the Warp Effects

A table of six possible random outcomes when psykers fail in the Psychic Maelstrom, ranging from mortal wounds to possession or transformation.

**Also known as:** D6 Result Effects on Psykers, Psychic Perils

**Tags:** psychic, warp effects, random event

**Related:** Battlezone: Psychic Maelstrom, Psychic Powers, Dark Imperium, The Emperor

---

#### Battlezone: Psychic Maelstrom

A hazardous environment where uncontrolled psykers create warp energy distortions causing random negative effects on psychic powers and psykers themselves.

**Also known as:** Psychic Maelstrom

**Tags:** battlezone, warp, psychic, environmental effect

**Related:** Perils of the Warp Effects, Dark Imperium, Great Rift, Warp Storms

---

#### Command Points (CPs)

A resource that players can spend to activate special Stratagems during the game, allowing for tactical advantages or additional actions.

**Also known as:** CPs, CP

**Tags:** resource, game mechanic, stratagem activation, game resources, power usage, resources, game mechanics, stratagems, stratagem, strategy, Gameplay Mechanic, Multiplayer

**Related:** Stratagems, Battle-forged Armies, Open Play

---

#### Warlord Trait: Insane Bravado

A warlord trait that allows the Warlord and friendly units within 8 inches to ignore Morale tests.

**Also known as:** Insane Bravado

**Tags:** warlord trait, morale, buff

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Meteoric Debris

A battlefield hazard where three dice numbered 1, 2, and 3 are placed at least 12 inches apart, and matching a rolled dice causes a flaming chunk to crash at that location dealing D3 mortal wounds to units within 6 inches.

**Also known as:** Meteoric Debris Hazard

**Tags:** game mechanic, battlefield hazard, shooting phase

**Related:** Orbital Bombardment Stratagem, State of the Imperium

---

#### Transport

A model or unit capable of carrying other units (embarked units), which arrive together with the transport on the battlefield.

**Tags:** unit types, vehicles, unit type, game mechanics, Warhammer 40,000

**Related:** Transport (Deployment), Adeptus Astartes

---

#### INFANTRY Model

A model representing infantry units capable of performing specific actions like carrying the Relic.

**Tags:** unit types

**Related:** Open Play

---

#### Turn

A player’s phase of play during which they perform actions such as deploying units, moving, shooting, and activating objectives.

**Tags:** game flow

**Related:** Battle Round, Core Rules

---

#### Round

A complete cycle of turns by both players that progresses battle time and may trigger checks for battle continuation or effects.

**Tags:** game flow, turn order

---

#### Defend Objectives

Tactical Objectives that require controlling a specified objective marker at the end of two consecutive turns to score victory points.

**Tags:** Tactical Objectives, scoring

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Capture and Control / Take and Hold

Tactical Objectives where players score victory points by controlling specified objective markers at the end of their turn.

**Also known as:** Take and Hold

**Tags:** Tactical Objectives, scoring

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Control (in Tactical Objectives)

For many Tactical Objectives, controlling an objective marker means having more models within 3 inches of its center than the opponent.

**Tags:** game mechanics, scoring

**Related:** Control (of an Objective Marker)

---

#### New Orders (Stratagem)

A Stratagem that allows a player to discard a generated Tactical Objective and immediately generate a new one, used after Tactical Objectives are rolled.

**Tags:** Stratagem, game mechanics

**Related:** Stratagems, Generating Tactical Objectives

---

#### Discarding Tactical Objectives

Removing Tactical Objectives from active play either after achievement or voluntarily with no points scored, preventing further generation or achievement.

**Also known as:** Objective Discarding

**Tags:** game mechanics, objectives, Game Mechanic, Strategy

---

#### Tactical Objective Cards

A deck of cards that can be used as an alternative method to dice rolling for generating Tactical Objectives, with cards kept face up for player visibility.

**Tags:** game components, randomization

**Related:** Generating Tactical Objectives

---

#### Major Victory

A decisive outcome in battle where either the Defender escapes with units totaling one third or more of their army's Power Level or the Attacker wins otherwise.

**Tags:** game results, victory conditions, game outcome, victory condition, Gameplay, Warhammer 40,000

**Related:** Victory Conditions

---

#### Relic

A unique objective marker representing an irreplaceable artefact placed at the battlefield center, crucial for specific scenario victory conditions.

**Also known as:** Relic Marker

**Tags:** objective marker, scenario-specific objective

**Related:** Tactical Priority

---

#### Objective Marker Placement

The process and rules governing how objective markers are set up on the battlefield, including distance restrictions from edges.

**Tags:** game setup, battlefield

**Related:** Deployment Zone

---

#### Linebreaker

A victory condition that grants 1 victory point if a player has at least one model positioned within the enemy’s deployment zone at the end of the battle.

**Tags:** victory conditions, scoring, victory condition, positioning, objectives, territory control, Warhammer 40k, deployment

---

#### First Blood

A victory condition awarding 1 victory point to the opposing player when the first unit is destroyed; if multiple are destroyed simultaneously, both players gain 1 point.

**Tags:** victory conditions, scoring, victory condition, combat, objectives, Warhammer 40k, unit destruction, timing

---

#### Warlord

A specific designated leader or character model within an army that holds special significance; its death can trigger victory point conditions such as Slay the Warlord.

**Also known as:** Army Leader, Commander, Leader

**Tags:** unit types, gameplay, Warhammer 40,000, Units, Leadership, Unit Role, Special Rules, characters, victory conditions, Unit Type, Game Terminology, game mechanics, special character, Command

A class of units typically equipped with heavy weapons, which influence control of objectives and scoring in specific conditions.

**Tags:** unit types, gameplay

A physical or symbolic marker placed on the battlefield that represents sites of tactical or strategic importance to be controlled for victory points.

#### Draw

A game result where neither player wins, typically because victory points are equal at battle end.

**Also known as:** Tie

**Tags:** game results, game outcome, scoring

**Related:** Victory Conditions

---

#### Battle Length

Defines the maximum number of battle rounds, with conditions for extending the game by rolling D6 at the end of certain rounds, and automatic game end after round 7.

**Also known as:** Random Battle Length

**Tags:** game mechanics, battle flow, timing, Warhammer 40k, time limit, game mechanic, time, battle phase, Warhammer 40,000, Game Duration

**Related:** D6, Dice Mechanics

#### Fight Phase

A phase in the game where units within 1 inch of an enemy can engage in combat by fighting, with specific rules governing the order and eligibility of unit fights during multiplayer play.

**Also known as:** Melee Phase, Close Combat Phase, Fight

**Tags:** Game Phase, Turn Sequence, Combat, game phases, Gameplay Phase

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

The phase in Warhammer 40,000 where units can declare charges to engage enemy units in close combat.

A unit of Space Marines outfitted with bolt rifles, often serving as frontline infantry.

A grenade weapon that has a Strength of 6 and AP of -1, inflicting D3 damage on a hit and effective against armored infantry like Intercessors.

#### Armor Penetration (AP)

A weapon attribute that reduces the target’s saving throw by a set amount, making it more difficult to save against wounds.

**Tags:** Weapon Characteristic, Combat Mechanic

**Related:** Krak Grenade, Weapons (Characteristics)

#### Save Characteristic

A numeric value representing a model's innate ability to resist damage, used in saving throw rolls against attacks after wounds are allocated.

**Also known as:** Save

**Tags:** Unit Characteristic, Defense, unit attribute, defense stat

---

#### Toughness

A unit characteristic representing how resilient a model is to attacks and used to determine the difficulty of wounding it.

**Tags:** Unit Characteristic, Combat

---

#### Strength (Weapon)

A weapon or attack characteristic used to determine how easily it wounds an enemy by comparing it to the target’s Toughness.

**Tags:** Weapon Characteristic, Combat

---

#### Ballistic Skill

A characteristic determining the dice roll needed to successfully hit a target with ranged weapons; e.g., 3+ means a roll of 3 or higher hits.

**Also known as:** BS

**Tags:** Unit Characteristic, Combat, unit attribute, combat stat

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Rapid Fire

A weapon special rule allowing a unit to fire twice if the target is within half the weapon’s maximum range.

**Tags:** Weapon Rule, Shooting Mechanic

**Related:** Boltgun

---

#### Boltgun

A standard firearm used by Space Marines and Plague Marines characterized by Strength 4, Rapid Fire 1, and inflicts 1 damage per successful wound.

**Also known as:** Bolter

**Tags:** Weapon, Ranged Weapon

**Related:** Rapid Fire, Intercessors, Adeptus Astartes Chapters, Bolter

---

#### Shooting Phase

The turn phase where units with ranged weapons select targets and fire, following specified rules about unit eligibility, range, line of sight, and weapon choice.

**Also known as:** Shooting Step, Ranged Combat Phase

**Tags:** Game Phase, Turn Sequence, Combat, game phases, turn structure, game mechanics, phases

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Psychic Phase

A game phase where psykers attempt to manifest psychic powers to aid allies or harm foes, with risks such as Perils of the Warp if tests fail.

**Also known as:** Phase of psychic powers

**Tags:** Game Phase, Turn Sequence, Psychic Powers, game phases, psychic abilities, turn structure

**Related:** Battle Round Phases

---

#### Movement Phase

The Movement Phase is the first phase of a battle round where players move their units on the battlefield according to their Move characteristics and constraints.

**Tags:** Game Phase, Turn Sequence, game phases, game mechanics, phases, turn structure

**Related:** Advance (Warhammer 40K), Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Advance (Warhammer 40K)

An optional additional movement in the Movement phase that allows units to move further but may have restrictions for shooting or other actions.

**Tags:** Game Mechanic, Movement

**Related:** Movement Phase, Adeptus Astartes

#### Dice Mechanics

Dice mechanics use six-sided dice (D6) to introduce randomness into game effects, including rolling multiple dice (e.g., 2D6) and interpreting results with modifiers.

**Also known as:** Dice Rolls, D6 Mechanics

**Tags:** game mechanics, randomness

#### Battle Round Phases

The ordered sequence of phases within a battle round: Movement, Psychic, Shooting, Charge, Fight, and Morale, each with specific actions players can take.

#### Battle Round

A discrete phase of the game in which players take turns performing actions; the game progresses through multiple battle rounds until specific conditions end it.

**Also known as:** Round

**Tags:** game phases, game mechanics, gameplay, turn, game phase, time measurement, round structure, game mechanic, Warhammer 40,000, turn structure

**Related:** Battle Round Phases, Turn, Tactical Priority

---

#### FLY

FLY is a keyword indicating models can move over other models and terrain as if they were not there, with minimum and maximum movement speeds applicable for flying movement.

**Also known as:** Flying

**Tags:** game mechanics, keywords, movement, unit ability

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Unit Coherency

Unit Coherency is a rule requiring that every model in a unit be within 2 inches horizontally and 6 inches vertically of at least one other model, maintaining formation integrity.

**Tags:** game mechanics, unit movement, rules

**Related:** Plague Marines

---

#### Random Value Characteristics

Some characteristics, like Move or Attacks, can be expressed as dice rolls (e.g., 2D6), requiring random dice rolls to determine actual values during play.

**Also known as:** Variable Characteristics

**Tags:** game mechanics, randomness, characteristics

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Modifiers

Modifiers are cumulative adjustments applied to characteristics, where multiplication/division is done before adding or subtracting values.

**Also known as:** Characteristic Modifiers

**Tags:** game mechanics, rules

**Related:** Dice Mechanics, Modifying Characteristics

**Tags:** game mechanics, equipment, Warhammer 40,000

**Related:** Weapons (Characteristics), Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Abilities

Abilities are special rules or effects unique to certain units that provide advantages or special options beyond the core game mechanics.

**Also known as:** Special Abilities, Unit Abilities

**Tags:** game mechanics, special rules

**Related:** Malignant Plaguecaster

---

#### Power Rating

Power Rating is a numerical value indicating the relative strength of a unit; the army’s Power Level is the sum of all units’ Power Ratings.

**Tags:** game mechanics, unit evaluation, army building, game balancing, matched play, unit attribute, Warhammer 40,000, game mechanic, army, unit stat, Gameplay, unit strength

---

#### Wounds (W)

Wounds represent the amount of damage a model can take before being defeated or removed from play.

**Also known as:** Hit Points

**Tags:** game mechanics, characteristics, health

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Toughness (T)

Toughness measures a model’s resilience to physical damage and its ability to resist wounds inflicted by enemy attacks.

**Tags:** game mechanics, characteristics, defense

**Related:** Characteristics

---

#### Strength (S)

Strength is a characteristic indicating how powerful a model’s melee attacks are, affecting the likelihood to wound opponents in close combat.

**Tags:** game mechanics, characteristics, combat

**Related:** Characteristics

---

#### Weapon Skill (WS)

Weapon Skill is a characteristic that measures a model’s proficiency in hand-to-hand combat, determining its ability to hit in melee fights.

**Also known as:** Melee Skill

**Tags:** game mechanics, characteristics, combat

**Related:** Characteristics

---

#### Move (M)

Move characteristic represents the speed, in inches, at which a model can move across the battlefield during the Movement Phase.

**Also known as:** Movement

**Tags:** game mechanics, characteristics, Warhammer 40,000

**Related:** Characteristics

---

#### Characteristics

Characteristics are numerical or descriptive values that define a model’s capabilities, such as movement speed, weapon skill, toughness, and wounds.

**Also known as:** Model Stats

**Tags:** game mechanics, attributes, Warhammer 40,000

**Related:** Move (M), Weapon Skill (WS), Ballistic Skill (BS), Strength (S), Toughness (T), Datasheet

---

#### Unit

A grouping of models that function together during gameplay in Warhammer 40,000 and have a minimum size stated on their datasheet.

**Also known as:** Model Unit, Squad, Group, Force

**Tags:** game mechanics, Warhammer 40,000, game units, gameplay, Game Entity, Models

**Related:** Aeldari Revenant Titans, Datasheet

---

#### Datasheet

A datasheet is a reference card listing the characteristics, wargear, and abilities for the models in a unit, defining their capabilities in the game.

**Also known as:** Unit Datasheet

**Tags:** game mechanics, reference, Warhammer 40,000, Rules, Unit Information

**Related:** Characteristics, Unit

---

#### Mortal Wounds

A type of damage that directly reduces a model's wounds and usually cannot be saved against, such as those caused by Perils of the Warp or Smite power.

**Tags:** damage types, combat, damage type, Warhammer 40,000, game mechanics

**Related:** Smite Power, Perils of the Warp, Psychic Powers

---

#### Roll D6

Rolling a six-sided die used frequently in game mechanics such as hit rolls, wound rolls, damage, and determining turn order.

**Also known as:** d6 roll, six-sided die roll

**Tags:** dice mechanics, game mechanics

**Related:** Dice Mechanics

---

#### Pistol Weapon

A ranged weapon that can be fired even if enemy units are within 1 inch and must target the closest enemy; models with pistols and other weapons must choose to fire pistols only or non-pistols only each shooting phase.

**Tags:** weapon types, ranged weapons, combat

**Related:** Weapon Types (Ranged)

---

#### Grenade Weapon

A weapon type allowing one model per unit to throw a grenade instead of firing a ranged weapon during the shooting phase.

**Tags:** weapon types, ranged weapons, combat

**Related:** Weapon Types (Ranged)

---

#### Rapid Fire Weapon

A ranged weapon type that can make double the number of attacks if the target is within half its maximum range.

**Tags:** weapon types, ranged weapons, combat

**Related:** Weapon Types (Ranged)

---

#### Heavy Weapon

Large, powerful ranged weapons requiring setup, that impose a -1 penalty to hit rolls if the model moved that turn.

**Tags:** weapon types, ranged weapons, combat

**Related:** Weapon Types (Ranged), Advance

---

#### Assault Weapon

A ranged weapon type that can be fired even if the model advanced during the turn, but suffers a -1 penalty to hit rolls after advancing.

**Tags:** weapon types, ranged weapons, combat

**Related:** Weapon Types (Ranged), Advance

---

#### Weapon Types (Ranged)

Five categories of ranged weapons are Assault, Heavy, Rapid Fire, Grenade, and Pistol, each with unique firing rules and effects on number of attacks and hit chances.

**Also known as:** Ranged Weapon Categories

**Tags:** weapons, combat, game mechanics

**Related:** Assault Weapon, Heavy Weapon, Rapid Fire Weapon, Grenade Weapon, Pistol Weapon

---

#### Aura Ability

Special abilities originating from certain units, usually characters, that affect friendly models within a set range, often including the unit with the ability itself.

**Also known as:** Aura Effect, Area Buff

**Tags:** abilities, aura effects, game mechanics

**Related:** Character (Model Type), Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Character (Model Type)

A hero, officer, prophet, or warlord model in the game, marked as CHARACTER, which has special targeting rules and sometimes has 10 or more wounds due to size.

**Also known as:** Hero, Warlord, Officer

**Tags:** model types, game units, targeting rules

**Related:** Aura Ability, Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Line of Sight

A visibility requirement for targeting in shooting; the shooter must be able to see the target, including through other models within its own unit, to engage in ranged attacks.

**Also known as:** LOS

**Tags:** targeting, game mechanics, combat

---

#### Sequencing (Rules Order)

The principle that when multiple rules trigger simultaneously, the player whose turn it is decides the order of their application; if before or after the battle or round, players roll off to decide.

**Also known as:** Rule Sequence, Order of Operations

**Tags:** game mechanics, rules resolution, conflict resolution

**Related:** Roll-off, Battle Round Phases

---

#### Psychic Sequence

The ordered steps during the psychic phase which include choosing a psyker and power, making a psychic test, the enemy attempting a deny the witch test, and resolving the power if successful.

**Also known as:** Psychic Phase Steps

**Tags:** psychic powers, game phases, turn structure

**Related:** Deny the Witch Test, Smite Power, Perils of the Warp, Battle Round Phases

---

#### Deny the Witch Test

A reactive psychic test rolled by a psyker within 24 inches of an enemy's manifested psychic power to resist and negate that power by beating the original psychic test roll.

**Also known as:** Deny the Witch, Counter Psychic Test

**Tags:** psychic powers, counterplay, dice rolls

**Related:** Psychic Sequence

---

#### Smite Power

A psychic power with a warp charge value of 5, which if successfully manifested, inflicts D3 mortal wounds on the closest visible enemy unit within 18 inches, or D6 mortal wounds if the psychic test result exceeds 10.

**Also known as:** Smite

**Tags:** psychic powers, game mechanics, damage

**Related:** Mortal Wounds, Psychic Sequence, Psychic Powers

---

#### Perils of the Warp

A hazardous event occurring when a psyker rolls double 1 or double 6 on a psychic test, causing D3 mortal wounds to the psyker and possibly to nearby units if the psyker is slain.

**Also known as:** Warp Perils, Warp hazard

**Tags:** psychic powers, damage, game mechanics

**Related:** Mortal Wounds, Psychic Sequence, Psychic Powers

---

#### Wobbly Models Syndrome

A rule addressing models that are unstable due to terrain; players must agree to safely balance such models to avoid toppling and must handle them properly when checking visibility or shooting.

**Also known as:** Model balancing, Terrain placement rules

**Tags:** gameplay, model placement, terrain interaction

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Unit Arrival

The process by which units enter the battlefield mid-turn, typically via teleportation or grav chutes, usually at the end of the Movement phase but sometimes during others. Units arriving cannot move or advance further that turn but can shoot or charge.

**Also known as:** Deploying units mid-turn

**Tags:** game mechanics, deployment, movement

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Aeldari, Units, Titans

#### Traps

A Defender Stratagem causing additional automatic casualties on replacement units arriving, by rolling dice for each model and inflicting deaths on rolls of 6.

**Tags:** Stratagem, defender, reinforcements

**Related:** Crucible of War: Ambush!, Defender

---

#### Foxholes

A Defender Stratagem that halves the number of hits sustained by an Infantry unit during Preliminary Bombardment, rounding up.

**Tags:** Stratagem, defender, combat mitigation

**Related:** Crucible of War: Ambush!, Defender

---

#### Decoys

A defender stratagem that allows placing two extra markers as decoys before set-up markers are placed; these markers are removed when revealed.

**Tags:** Stratagem, defender, deception, defender stratagem, deployment

**Related:** Concealed Deployment, Defender

---

#### Spies

An Attacker Stratagem used to force the Defender to reveal one hidden unit at a setup marker immediately after deployment.

**Tags:** Stratagem, scouting, attacker

**Related:** Attacker

---

#### Sustained Bombardment

An Attacker Stratagem that allows rolling three dice instead of one to determine hits during Preliminary Bombardment.

**Tags:** Stratagem, combat, attacker

**Related:** Dice Mechanics

---

#### Random Battle Length

A rule that extends a battle past the fixed rounds based on dice rolls at the end of certain battle rounds, with a maximum limit for automatic ending.

**Tags:** game mechanics, battle duration, game mechanic, narrative play

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Troops Battlefield Role

#### Sustained Assault

A mission feature representing the Attacker's numerical superiority, requiring replacement units to deploy wholly within 6 inches of the Attacker's battlefield edge, with no holding back on bringing units in.

**Tags:** game mechanics, reinforcements, Attacker, mission rule, deployment, strategy

**Related:** Troops Battlefield Role, Outflanking Reinforcements, Defender

#### Temporary Comms Uplink Stratagem

A Stratagem costing 3 Command Points that allows a player with fewer than six active Tactical Objectives to immediately generate 1 extra Tactical Objective.

**Tags:** stratagem, tactics, command points

**Related:** Stratagem

---

#### Stratagem

Special tactical options players can activate by spending Command Points to gain advantages, perform special actions, or influence the game state.

**Also known as:** Stratagems, Tactical Stratagem

**Tags:** game mechanics, tactics, resources, abilities, strategy, Game Mechanic, Resource Management, special ability, Gameplay Mechanic, Ability, Multiplayer

**Related:** Silenced Weapons stratagem, Scan for Distress Beacons stratagem, Night Raid stratagem, Sensors stratagem, Rapid Response stratagem, Extra Sentries stratagem, Temporary Comms Uplink Stratagem

---

#### Steal the Loot

A victory condition awarding 1 additional victory point at game end to the player who has achieved more ‘Secure Objective X’ Tactical Objectives than their opponent.

**Tags:** victory condition, objectives, scoring

**Related:** Precious Cargo

---

#### Precious Cargo

A mission rule allowing both players to achieve any active Tactical Objective titled ‘Secure Objective X’; these objectives can only be discarded upon being achieved.

**Tags:** mission rule, objectives, tactical

**Related:** Steal the Loot, Tactical Priority

---

#### Tactical Priority (Mission Priorities Variation)

An endgame scoring condition granting 1 additional victory point if a player has achieved more Tactical Objectives of their nominated type than their opponent.

**Also known as:** Mission Priorities

**Tags:** victory conditions, scoring, objectives

**Related:** Tactical Priority

---

#### Tactical Priority

A rule where each player nominates a tactical objective type at the start of battle; they score extra points for achieving objectives of that type but lose points when discarding them.

**Tags:** game mechanics, scoring, objectives

#### Extra Sentries stratagem

A Defender stratagem enabling two units to be set up as Sentries instead of one before setting up Sentries.

**Tags:** stratagem, defender, tactics, setup

**Related:** Stratagem

---

#### Rapid Response stratagem

A Defender stratagem that allows a unit to arrive automatically as Reserve without a dice roll after the alarm, excluding deployment near the Attacker’s battlefield edge.

**Tags:** stratagem, defender, tactics, deployment

**Related:** Stratagem

---

#### Sensors stratagem

A Defender stratagem that increases the spotting range of Sentry units by 3" after they are set up.

**Tags:** stratagem, defender, tactics, game mechanics

**Related:** Stratagem

---

#### Night Raid stratagem

An Attacker stratagem invoked after deployment that applies Dawn Raid rules and halves Sentry spotting ranges during the first battle round.

**Tags:** stratagem, attacker, tactics, game mechanics

**Related:** Stratagem, Dawn Raid rules

---

#### Scan for Distress Beacons stratagem

An Attacker stratagem used at the end of the Movement phase allowing a dice roll to potentially find the Spy if a model is within 12" of unexplored terrain.

**Tags:** stratagem, attacker, tactics

**Related:** Stratagem, Victory conditions in Rescue Mission

---

#### Silenced Weapons stratagem

An Attacker stratagem that allows a shooting attack to avoid triggering the alarm if the target is wounded but not killed.

**Tags:** stratagem, attacker, tactics, game mechanics

**Related:** Stratagem

---

#### Victory conditions in Rescue Mission

The criteria determining the winner, where the Attacker wins if the Spy is discovered and alive at battle end; otherwise, the Defender wins.

**Tags:** game mechanics, objectives, victory

**Related:** Scan for Distress Beacons stratagem

---

#### Battle length (Random Battle Length rules)

A rule determining the duration of the battle using randomized conditions from a reference page, influencing when the battle ends.

**Also known as:** Random Battle Length

**Tags:** game mechanics, game duration

**Related:** Finding the Spy, Battle Round Phases

---

#### Finding the Spy

A procedure where a dice roll is made when an Attacker’s model moves within 3" of potential Spy locations; success results in placing the Spy or ending the battle if placement is impossible.

**Also known as:** Spy discovery

**Tags:** game mechanics, objectives, dice rolls

**Related:** Battle length (Random Battle Length rules), Defender’s Reserves

---

#### Defender’s Reserves

Reserves specific to the defending side who can enter the battlefield after the alarm sounds, often requiring a dice roll on the first turn and restricted to deployment zones away from enemy models.

**Tags:** game mechanics, deployment, defender

**Related:** Finding the Spy, Defender

---

**Tags:** fictional deity, Aeldari mythology, Warhammer 40k, Deity

**Related:** Fall (of the Aeldari)

---

#### Fall (of the Aeldari)

The catastrophic event in Aeldari history where their gods were slain and devoured by Slaanesh, fracturing their civilization and leaving their souls vulnerable.

**Tags:** fictional event, Warhammer 40K lore, history

**Related:** Daemon, Cegorach

#### Dedicated Transport

#### Spearhead Detachment

A Detachment focused on elite units, granting +1 Command Point, restricted to same Faction, with limited numbers across Battlefield Roles.

**Tags:** detachment type, army composition

**Related:** Detachment

---

#### Vanguard Detachment

A Detachment emphasizing heavy support units, granting +1 Command Point and limited to same Faction, with specified unit maximums and minimums.

**Tags:** detachment type, army composition

**Related:** Detachment

---

#### Patrol Detachment

A smaller Detachment type with fewer compulsory units, granting +1 Command Point and restricted to single Faction units.

**Tags:** detachment type, army composition, battle-forged

**Related:** Detachment

---

#### Brigade Detachment

A Detachment allowing a flexible unit composition with a large number of Battlefield Role slots, granting +3 Command Points and same Faction restriction.

**Tags:** detachment type, army composition, battle-forged

**Related:** Detachment

---

#### Battalion Detachment

A Detachment type requiring several compulsory units from multiple Battlefield Roles, granting +9 Command Points and restrictions to same Faction.

**Tags:** detachment type, army composition, battle-forged

**Related:** Detachment

---

#### Insane Bravery Stratagem

A Stratagem used before taking a Morale test that allows automatic passing of that single test at a Command Point cost.

**Tags:** stratagem, morale, game mechanics

**Related:** Stratagems

---

#### Counter-Offensive Stratagem

A Stratagem used after an enemy unit finishes a charge attack, allowing the player to select an eligible unit to fight next.

**Tags:** stratagem, combat tactic

**Related:** Stratagems

---

#### Command Re-roll Stratagem

A Stratagem allowing the player to re-roll any single dice result during the game.

**Tags:** stratagem, dice mechanic, game tactics

**Related:** Stratagems

---

Bonuses granted by including certain Detachments in an army, often impacting resources like Command Points.

#### Map Campaign

A campaign style using a geographical grid or Realm of Battle board where territories are captured or lost based on battle outcomes, including additional rules like supply and reinforcements.

**Tags:** campaign type, game structure, geography, Narrative, Territory Control

**Related:** Campaigns

---

#### Matrix Campaign

A campaign format involving secret player choices that determine the mission and attacker/defender roles for each battle, using a pre-defined matrix to cross-reference decisions.

**Tags:** campaign type, game structure, Strategic Planning, Narrative

**Related:** Campaigns

---

#### Tree Campaign

A campaign type where each battle’s outcome determines the next mission in a branching chain, with unique effects applying to subsequent games.

**Tags:** campaign type, game structure, Narrative, Linked Games

**Related:** Campaigns

---

#### Campaigns

A series of linked battles with recurring themes and impacts where players create heroes and legends that influence the broader war.

**Also known as:** War Campaigns

**Tags:** wargaming, game mode, series

**Related:** Tree Campaign, Matrix Campaign, Map Campaign, Carnage Mission, State of the Imperium

#### Flares

A Stratagem that costs 1 Command Point and allows units to shoot at a selected enemy without penalty from the Cover of Darkness rule for the rest of the turn.

**Tags:** stratagem, game mechanics, Warhammer 40k

**Related:** Cover of Darkness, Strategic Deadlock

---

#### Cover of Darkness

A game rule that imposes a penalty of subtracting 1 from hit rolls when shooting at targets farther than 18 inches away.

**Tags:** game mechanics, shooting rules, Warhammer 40k

**Related:** Flares

A game mechanic where Tactical Objectives are kept hidden from opponents until they are achieved.

#### Inquisitorial Representative

A temporary seat held by whoever the Inquisition assigns for each session rather than a fixed Inquisitor, representing the Inquisition's interests.

**Also known as:** Inquisition Representative

**Tags:** Imperium governance, Offices, Warhammer 40k lore

**Related:** High Lords of Terra

---

#### Earth Cracks

A Fire and Fury rule causing units beginning their turn entirely within terrain features to have halved move characteristics and imposing mortal wound risks when charging through such terrain; flying units are unaffected.

**Tags:** gaming, battlezone, movement, hazards

**Related:** Fire and Fury Battlezone

---

#### Burning Skies

A Fire and Fury rule where flying units roll a dice after movement and suffer mortal wounds on a roll of 1 due to hazardous falling debris.

**Tags:** gaming, battlezone, unit hazard, flyers

**Related:** Fire and Fury Battlezone

---

#### Fire and Fury Battlezone

A battlezone simulating combat in extreme conditions involving cataclysmic battles and environmental hazards that affect movement, cause mortal wounds, and halve move values in terrain.

**Tags:** gaming, battlezone, environment, hazards

**Related:** Burning Skies, Earth Cracks, Battlescape, Objective Marker Effects (D6 Result Effects)

---

#### Objective Marker Effects (D6 Result Effects)

Random effects applied to objective markers decided by dice rolls, such as causing mortal wounds, granting re-roll abilities, or modifying charge distances.

**Also known as:** Objective Marker Random Effects

**Tags:** gaming, objectives, random effects

**Related:** Fire and Fury Battlezone

---

#### Stratagem - Light ’Em Up

A stratagem allowing a player to shoot at a selected enemy unit without incurring penalties from Low Visibility during their turn.

**Also known as:** Light ’Em Up

**Tags:** gaming, stratagem, combat

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Delayed Arrival (Reserves)

A Night Fight rule where units arriving from reserves must roll on a dice; results of 1 or 2 delay their entrance by one turn.

**Tags:** gaming, game mechanic, reserve units

**Related:** Night Fight Battlezone

---

#### Low Visibility (Shooting Penalties)

A rule in Night Fight where hit rolls suffer penalties at increasing distance thresholds: no penalty at 0-12", -1 at 12-24", -2 at 24-36", and -3 beyond 36".

**Also known as:** Visibility Shooting Penalty

**Tags:** gaming, combat mechanics, shooting

**Related:** Night Fight Battlezone

---

#### Night Fight Battlezone

A battlezone simulating low or zero visibility conditions that imposes shooting penalties by distance and causes delayed arrivals of reserve units via dice rolls.

**Tags:** gaming, battlezone, visibility, shooting penalty

**Related:** Low Visibility (Shooting Penalties), Delayed Arrival (Reserves), Battlezones, Dawn Raid, Crucible of War: Ambush!

---

#### Hills

Elevated battlefield features that provide commanding views but do not confer cover benefits; large hills may block line of sight.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, line of sight, cover

**Related:** Battlescape, Scratch-Built Terrain

---

#### Scratch-Built Terrain

Player-created terrain features not covered by official rules that require custom agreed-upon rulings, enhancing creativity and unique battlefield experiences.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, custom rules, hobby

**Related:** Hills

---

#### Battlescape

A terrain feature including smoking hulls and blasted trees that provide cover as woods do but pose mine hazards causing mortal wounds on a dice roll of 1 when charging or advancing.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, cover, hazards

**Related:** Fire and Fury Battlezone, Hills

---

#### Mortal Wound

A damage type that inflicts one point of damage per wound directly without a wound roll or saving throw, and excess mortal wounds can be allocated to other models in a unit.

**Also known as:** Instant Damage

**Tags:** gaming, damage types, special damage, combat mechanic, damage type, game mechanics

**Related:** Fuel Pipes

---

#### Fuel Pipes

Armored pipes that follow barricade cover rules but add a hazard causing mortal wounds on a failed saving throw roll of 1 during the shooting phase.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, hazard, cover

**Related:** Mortal Wound, Barricades

---

#### Leadership

A unit characteristic influencing morale and command-related effects, which can be increased by terrain like Imperial Statuary.

**Tags:** gaming, unit characteristics, morale

**Related:** Imperial Statuary

---

#### Imperial Statuary

Terrain pieces representing heroes of the Imperium that grant cover to units partially obscured within 3" and increase Leadership by +1 for Imperial units within the same range.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, cover, leadership

**Related:** Leadership, Cover

---

#### Titanic Models

Very large models immune to slowed movement penalties caused by obstacles.

**Tags:** gaming, unit type, special rules

**Related:** Obstacles (Tank Traps and Tanglewire), Dice Mechanics

---

#### Obstacles (Tank Traps and Tanglewire)

Two types of terrain that halve movement for units advancing or charging over them, except Titanic models which are unaffected; tank traps affect Vehicles and Monsters, tanglewire affects other units.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, movement, obstacles

**Related:** Titanic Models, Battlefield Terrain Features

---

#### Craters

Terrain features formed by bombardment that grant cover to infantry units fully within them and slow charging units by reducing charge distance by 2".

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, cover, movement

**Related:** Cover

---

#### Barricades

Makeshift defensive terrain providing cover to infantry within 1" behind them and allowing units to fight across barricades up to 2" apart.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, cover, combat

**Related:** Cover, Fuel Pipes

---

#### Ruins (Terrain)

Remains of cities providing cover to infantry and partially to other units, restricting non-flying units such as Flyers, Vehicles, Monsters, and Bikes to the ground floor.

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, cover, movement restrictions

**Related:** Cover, Flyers

---

#### Woods (Terrain)

Twisted woodland terrain that provides infantry units cover when entirely on its base and slows charging units by subtracting 2" from charge distance.

**Also known as:** Forest

**Tags:** gaming, terrain, cover, movement

**Related:** Cover

---

#### Cover

Terrain features that provide defensive benefits, granting units +1 to saving throws against shooting attacks when completely on or within terrain but excluding invulnerable saves and no benefit in Fight phase.

**Tags:** gaming, combat mechanics, terrain effects, terrain mechanic, defense bonus, game environment, game mechanics, combat

**Related:** Woods (Terrain), Ruins (Terrain), Craters, Barricades, Imperial Statuary

---

#### Supreme Command Detachment

A detachment composed mainly of HQ units (3-5), optionally Elites and Lord of War, requires units from the same faction, grants +1 Command Point, but loses Command Points per Auxiliary Support Detachment.

**Tags:** gaming, army composition, detachment, command point

**Related:** Command Point (CP)

---

#### Air Wing Detachment

A detachment type allowing 3-5 Flyers with no faction or command point restrictions.

**Tags:** gaming, army composition, detachment, Flyers

**Related:** Flyers

---

#### Flyers

Unit type capable of flight, often limited in number per detachment and interacting differently with terrain and battlefield hazards.

**Also known as:** Flying Units

**Tags:** gaming, unit type, mobility

**Related:** Air Wing Detachment, Ruins (Terrain)

---

#### Super-Heavy Detachment

A detachment that includes one Lord of War and has no faction or command point restrictions.

**Tags:** gaming, army composition, detachment, Lord of War

**Related:** Lord of War

---

#### Lord of War

A powerful, often game-changing unit typically restricted to one per detachment that significantly impacts army capabilities.

**Tags:** gaming, unit type, powerful unit

**Related:** Auxiliary Detachment, Super-Heavy Detachment, Adeptus Astartes Chapters

---

#### Auxiliary Detachment

A detachment with no faction or command point restrictions that includes a single Lord of War unit.

**Tags:** gaming, army composition, detachment, Lord of War

**Related:** Lord of War

---

#### Fortification Network

A detachment composed of 1-3 fortification units from the same faction, granting +1 Command Point.

**Tags:** gaming, army composition, detachment, fortifications

**Related:** Command Point (CP)

---

#### Auxiliary Support Detachment

A detachment type requiring all units be from the same faction and granting +3 Command Points but with no unit composition restrictions.

**Tags:** gaming, army composition, detachment

**Related:** Command Point (CP)

---

#### Command Point (CP)

A resource earned or spent during gameplay that grants various strategic benefits, with specific detachments providing bonuses to the total amount.

**Also known as:** CP

**Tags:** gaming, resource management

**Related:** Outrider Detachment, Fortification Network, Auxiliary Support Detachment, Supreme Command Detachment

---

#### Outrider Detachment

A type of army detachment requiring all units to be from the same faction, providing +1 Command Point and allowing dedicated transports. Its composition limits HQ, Troops, Elites, Fast Attack, Heavy Support, and Flyers units.

**Tags:** gaming, army composition, detachment, command point

**Related:** Command Point (CP)

---

#### Dice

Physical or digital polyhedral tools used to introduce randomness into game outcomes such as Tactical Objective generation or initiative determination.

**Also known as:** Die, Random Number Generator

**Tags:** Game Component, Randomization

**Related:** Tactical Objectives

---

#### Mission of Utmost Importance

A Tactical Objective that immediately generates a bonus Tactical Objective scored only by the player's Warlord, granting both the victory points from the bonus objective and 3 additional points; discarding discards both.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Bonus Objective, Warlord

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Maintain Air Superiority

A Tactical Objective earning 1 victory point if at least one enemy unit that can fly is destroyed.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Combat, Unit Ability

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Destroy Enemy Units in Fight Phase

A Tactical Objective awarding 1 victory point for destroying an enemy unit during the Fight phase, or D3 points for destroying three or more units.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Combat Phase

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Destroy Large Enemy Units

A Tactical Objective awarding victory points for destroying enemy units with large wounds: 1 point for 10+ wounds units and D3 for 20+ wounds units.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Combat

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Control Battlefield Centre

A Tactical Objective that scores 1 victory point if no enemy models are within 6 inches of the battlefield center, or D3 points if none are within 12 inches at turn end.

**Also known as:** Centre Control

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Area Control

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Eliminate Enemy Psykers

A Tactical Objective awarding 1 victory point if at least one enemy Psyker is destroyed during the turn.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Targeted Elimination

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Assassinate Enemy Characters

A Tactical Objective awarding victory points for destroying enemy Characters: 1 point for one Character or D3 points for three or more in a single turn.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Targeted Elimination

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Exterminate Enemy Units

A Tactical Objective awarding victory points based on the number of enemy units destroyed during the player's turn: 1 point for one unit, D3 for 3-5, D3+3 for 6 or more.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Combat

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Kill the Enemy Warlord

A Tactical Objective awarding D3 victory points if the opponent’s Warlord has been destroyed during this or any previous turn.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Target Elimination

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Enemy Units Destroyed (Shooting)

A Tactical Objective awarding 1 victory point for destroying an enemy unit during the Shooting phase, or D3 points for destroying three or more units.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Combat Phase

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Defend Objective 6

A Tactical Objective scoring D3+3 victory points if a player controls every objective marker on the battlefield at turn's end.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Control

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Mission Critical Objective

A Tactical Objective scored by having at least three units completely within your deployment zone and no opponent models there at turn's end; cannot be scored on the first turn.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Unit Positioning

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Domination

A primary objective where each objective marker controlled at the end of every turn awards 1 victory point, accumulating throughout the battle.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Control, Warhammer 40,000, Primary Objectives, Victory Conditions

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Supremacy

A Tactical Objective scoring victory points for having units completely within the enemy’s deployment zone: 1 point for one unit, D3 points for at least three units.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Unit Positioning

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Hold the Line

A Tactical Objective where players roll a D6 to determine an objective marker; controlling that marker grants 1 victory point or D3 points if captured from an opponent during that turn.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Randomization

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Advance Behind Enemy Lines

A Tactical Objective scored by having no units from your army within your deployment zone at the end of your turn, earning 1 victory point.

**Tags:** Tactical Objective, Mission

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Bonus Tactical Objective

An additional Tactical Objective that is generated during a mission and does not count towards the active objectives but grants extra victory points if achieved.

**Also known as:** Bonus Objective

**Tags:** Game Mechanic, Optional Objective

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Terrain

Physical or represented features on the battlefield that influence movement and tactical decisions during a Warhammer 40,000 game.

**Tags:** Battlefield Element, Game Environment, Warhammer 40,000, Battlefield

**Related:** Control an Objective Marker

---

#### Psychic Power

A special ability manifested or denied by Psykers during a turn, which can contribute to victory points when used.

**Tags:** Ability, Game Mechanic

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Character

A special type of unit or model with unique abilities or rules, often important in achieving Tactical Objectives.

**Also known as:** Hero, Special Unit

**Tags:** Unit Type, Gameplay

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Active Tactical Objective

A Tactical Objective currently in play that can be achieved or discarded by a player during the game.

**Also known as:** Current Tactical Objective

**Tags:** Game State, Game Mechanic

**Related:** Tactical Objective

---

#### Control an Objective Marker

Having more models within 3 inches of the objective marker’s center than your opponent, thus gaining control of that marker.

**Also known as:** Objective Control

**Tags:** Game Mechanics, Control

**Related:** Terrain

#### Character Model

Models that are identified as heroes or leaders with special abilities, such as performing Heroic Interventions during the enemy charge phase.

**Tags:** unit type, game classification

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes, Heroic Intervention

---

#### Disembark

The action of a unit leaving a transport before it moves, requiring set up within 3 inches of the transport and not within 1 inch of enemies; models unable to be placed this way are slain.

**Tags:** game procedure, movement

---

#### Embark

The action of moving a unit into a friendly transport by ending movement within 3 inches of the transport, removing the unit from play until disembarked or the transport is destroyed.

**Tags:** game procedure, movement

---

#### Transport Capacity

A numerical limit specifying how many and what types of models a transport vehicle can carry, as indicated on its datasheet.

**Tags:** game statistic, unit property

**Related:** Transport Vehicle

---

#### Consolidate

A post-combat movement where models may move up to 3 inches closer to the nearest enemy model.

**Tags:** movement, combat procedure

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Melee Weapon

A type of weapon used in close combat, characterized by stats such as range, type, strength, armour penetration, and damage, which may be chosen from a model's datasheet or defaulted if none are listed.

**Also known as:** Close Combat Weapon

**Tags:** weapon type, combat equipment

**Related:** Number of Attacks Characteristic, Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Number of Attacks Characteristic

A model’s attribute indicating how many close combat attacks it can perform when fighting.

**Also known as:** Attacks

**Tags:** unit attribute, combat stat

**Related:** Melee Weapon, Dice Mechanics

---

#### Charge

A special movement phase where eligible units move towards enemy units within 12 inches to engage in close combat, including potential enemy Overwatch fire and a 2D6 charge move distance roll.

**Tags:** game phase, movement, combat, Gameplay Action

**Related:** Heroic Intervention, Tactical Priority

---

#### Invulnerable Save

A special saving throw available to some models that ignores Armour Penetration and can be chosen instead of the normal save, but only one invulnerable save may be used per wound.

**Tags:** defense mechanic, special ability

**Related:** Armour Penetration, Dice Mechanics

---

#### Damage Characteristic

A value indicating how many wounds a weapon inflicts per successful attack if not prevented by saves.

**Tags:** weapon attribute, combat stat

**Related:** Adeptus Astartes

---

#### Armour Penetration

A weapon's characteristic that reduces the effectiveness of the target model's save by modifying the saving throw roll.

**Also known as:** AP

**Tags:** weapon attribute, combat stat, defense penetration

**Related:** Invulnerable Save, Dice Mechanics

---

#### Allocate Wound

The process where the defending player assigns incoming wounds to specific models within a unit, prioritizing models already wounded.

**Tags:** combat procedure, gameplay mechanic

---

#### Toughness Characteristic

A numeric value representing a model's resilience or ability to resist damage, used in conjunction with Strength to calculate wound probability.

**Tags:** unit attribute, combat stat

---

#### Strength Characteristic

A numeric value representing how powerful or forceful an attack is, used in combat to compare against the target's Toughness to determine wound success.

**Tags:** unit attribute, combat stat

**Related:** Trance Broadcast, Astropathic Corps

#### Warp entities

Mischievous or malevolent psychic beings existing within the Warp that can interfere with psychic messages by altering, contaminating, or piggybacking on them.

---

Powerful psychic reverberations caused by major warp events or cataclysms that can be unintentionally received by sensitive Astropaths, sometimes causing mental harm.

#### Raging warp storm

Intense, violent phenomena within the Warp that can redirect, swallow, or destroy psychic messages, sometimes blocking communication for centuries.

**Also known as:** Warp storm

**Tags:** science fiction, psychic phenomena, communication hazards

**Related:** Warp interference, Chaos

---

#### Warp interference

Disruptions to psychic messages traveling through the Warp caused by fluctuations like warp tides or overlapping telepathic signals.

**Also known as:** Warp noise, Psychic static

**Tags:** science fiction, psychic phenomena, communication obstacles

**Related:** Raging warp storm, Random chance in warp communication, Warp entities, Chaos

#### Astropath

**Related:** Scholastica Psykana, Astropathic Corps

---

#### Unit destruction

The removal of a unit from play when it is defeated, which may trigger victory points like First Blood or No Quarter Given.

**Also known as:** Unit kill, Elimination

**Tags:** game mechanics, combat outcome

**Related:** Tactical Priority

---

#### Model

A physical representation of a unit on the battlefield, used to measure control of objectives and positions.

**Also known as:** Unit model, Figure

**Tags:** game piece, measurement

---

#### Random selection

The process of choosing game elements, such as objective markers, by chance after setup or deployment phases.

**Also known as:** Random designation

**Tags:** game mechanics, setup, chance

---

#### Dice roll mechanic

Use of a six-sided die (D6) to resolve game events, such as determining initiative or whether the battle continues after set rounds.

**Tags:** game mechanics, random chance

**Related:** Dice Mechanics

---

#### Standard deployment map

Predefined battlefield layout specifying deployment zones and other setup details, referenced by page number.

**Tags:** battlefield, setup, game rules

---

#### Spy Model

A single model representing the spy in the Rescue Mission, not contributing to Power Level and treated as a single-unit; can only be targeted if closest.

**Also known as:** Spy

**Tags:** unit, special rule, mission

**Related:** Spy (in Rescue Mission), Reserve

---

#### Spy (in Rescue Mission)

An Infantry model representing a spy with up to 4 Wounds, not part of the Attacker’s battle-forged army Power Level and treated as a single model unit that can only be attacked if the closest target.

**Tags:** special unit, mission, infantry

**Related:** Spy Model

---

#### Extra Sentries

A Defender stratagem allowing two units to be set up as Sentries immediately before Sentry deployment instead of one.

**Tags:** defender stratagem, deployment

**Related:** Stratagems, Sentry

---

#### Cut the Wires

A Defender stratagem that reduces the number of Sabotage attempts made by the Attacker by 1 (minimum 0) if any unit is within 3 inches of the Objective at game end.

**Tags:** defender stratagem, sabotage, game effect

**Related:** Stratagems

---

#### Sensors

A Defender stratagem that adds 3 inches to Sentries’ spotting distances after they are set up.

**Tags:** defender stratagem, detection, unit capability

**Related:** Sentry

---

#### Camouflage

An Attacker stratagem that halves a unit’s Power Rating for distance spotting by Sentries during deployment setup.

**Tags:** attacker stratagem, stealth, deployment

**Related:** Stratagems

---

#### Extra Explosives

An Attacker stratagem allowing a unit to make one additional Sabotage attempt during the game after making an initial attempt.

**Tags:** attacker stratagem, sabotage, combat action

**Related:** State of the Imperium

---

#### Silenced Weapons

An Attacker stratagem used before resolving a shooting attack that causes the alarm to sound only if the target loses wounds but is not slain.

**Tags:** attacker stratagem, shooting attack, stealth

**Related:** State of the Imperium

---

#### Sabotage Attempt

An action by an Attacker unit within 3 inches of the Objective at the end of its turn to destroy the Objective, with restrictions that each unit may only attempt once and vehicles or monsters cannot attempt.

**Tags:** action, objective, mission

**Related:** Sabotage

---

#### Sentry

A unit designated to guard specific areas, with requirements such as number and position within the Defender's deployment zone, especially near the battlefield center.

**Also known as:** Sentries, Guard Unit

**Tags:** unit role, deployment, mission

**Related:** Extra Sentries, Sensors

---

#### Sabotage

A mission where the Attacker conducts a surprise raid to sneak past sentries, plant explosives to destroy an objective, while the Defender attempts to react if an alarm is raised.

**Also known as:** Sabotage Mission

**Tags:** mission, objectives, stealth, combat

**Related:** Sabotage Attempt, Crucible of War Missions, Asymmetrical Gameplay, Destroy any Approach (Victory Points), Break Through (Victory Points)

---

#### Destroy any Approach (Victory Points)

Victory points scored by the Defender for each Attacker unit destroyed during the battle, granting 1 point per unit.

**Tags:** victory condition, scoring, combat

**Related:** Sabotage

---

#### Break Through (Victory Points)

Victory points scored by the Attacker for having units at battle’s end with models completely within the Defender’s Front Line or Second Line deployment zones (1 point per unit in Front Line, 2 points per unit in Second Line).

**Tags:** victory condition, deployment zone, scoring

**Related:** Sabotage

---

#### Proximity Mines

A defender stratagem where, the first time an enemy unit moves into or through the Front Line deployment zone, a dice is rolled per model, and each roll of 6 slays one model in that unit.

**Tags:** defender stratagem, deployment zone, combat

**Related:** State of the Imperium

---

#### Dug-in Defences

A defender stratagem that adds +1 to a unit's saving throws against all shooting attacks until the unit moves.

**Tags:** defender stratagem, saving throw, defense

**Related:** State of the Imperium

---

#### Cover Ground

A rule allowing a unit to count its Advance roll as a six before rolling for its actual movement distance.

**Tags:** movement, game mechanic, strategy

---

#### Forced March

A deployment rule allowing a replacement unit to be set up anywhere within the Attacker's deployment zone more than 9 inches away from enemy units.

**Tags:** deployment, game mechanic, strategy

**Related:** Reserve

---

#### Going to Ground

A tactical choice available to infantry units under Preliminary Bombardment where they suffer fewer mortal wounds but cannot act on their first turn.

**Tags:** special rule, tactics, Warhammer 40,000

**Related:** Tactical Priority

---

#### Alarm Conditions

Specific triggers that cause the Sentries to raise an alarm, such as attackers firing ranged weapons, failing to kill a Sentry in combat, or being spotted.

**Tags:** game mechanic, narrative play, Warhammer 40,000

---

#### Reserves

Units that start the game off the battlefield and enter later at specified times or conditions during the battle.

**Tags:** game mechanic, deployment, Warhammer 40,000

**Related:** Reserve

Additional gameplay modifications or conditions applied to narrative missions to reflect specific tactics, strategies, or story elements.

**Related:** House Rules, Tactical Priority

#### Deployment Zones

Specified areas on the battlefield where players must initially place their units at the start of a game or mission.

#### Standard Deployment Maps

Six pre-defined battlefield layouts used in matched play missions chosen by dice roll to determine unit deployment zones and battle conditions.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40,000, Matched Play, Deployment

**Related:** Defender’s Battlefield Edge, Attacker’s Battlefield Edge, Battlefield Terrain Features

---

#### Tactical Reserves

A matched play rule requiring at least half of an army's units to be deployed on the battlefield at the start, with remaining units arriving later or counted as destroyed if not present by turn three.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40,000, Deployment, Matched Play Rules

**Related:** Rapid Reinforcements, Delayed Reserves, Signal the Attack, Tactical Priority

---

#### Strategic Discipline

A matched play rule preventing players from using the same Stratagem more than once in a single phase, with exceptions for Stratagems used outside normal phases.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40,000, Stratagems, Matched Play Rules

---

#### Psychic Focus

A matched play rule limiting each psychic power, except Smite, to be attempted only once per turn instead of once per psyker.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40,000, Psychic Powers, Matched Play Rules

**Related:** Stratagems

---

#### Crushing Victory

A type of decisive victory granted immediately upon opponent concession or elimination of all their battlefield units in Warhammer 40,000.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40,000, Victory Conditions

**Related:** Sudden Death Victory, Tactical Priority

---

#### Sudden Death Victory

A game-ending condition in Warhammer 40,000 where a player concedes or loses all battlefield models, immediately awarding a crushing victory to the opponent.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40,000, Victory Conditions, Gameplay

**Related:** Units Destroyed, Crushing Victory, Tactical Priority

---

A subset of points reserved in an army roster for summoning or adding units during battle, which decrement as units enter the battlefield.

#### Heavy Bombardment

Rules governing the use of the Preliminary Bombardment Stratagem including its effects and sequencing.

#### Units Destroyed

Enemy units not present on the battlefield at the end of the game, counted as destroyed for scoring Victory Points.

**Related:** Sudden Death Victory, Tactical Priority

---

#### Home Advantage

A Defender Stratagem used before deciding who takes the first turn, allowing a player to roll two dice and choose the higher result, costing Command Points.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Defender, turn order

---

#### Delayed Reserves

A Defender Stratagem that imposes penalties on an opponent’s Reserve roll by subtracting 1 or 2 from their dice roll, costing 1 or 2 Command Points.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Defender, Reserve rolls, counterplay

**Related:** Tactical Reserves, Defender

---

#### Rapid Reinforcements

A Defender Stratagem that lets a unit automatically arrive from Reserve without making a roll when about to roll for Reserve arrival, costing Command Points.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Defender, Reserve

**Related:** Tactical Reserves, Defender

---

#### Signal the Attack

An Attacker Stratagem used at the end of the Movement phase which adds +1 to every Reserve roll made for that turn, costing Command Points.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Attacker, Reserve rolls

**Related:** Tactical Reserves, Attacker

---

#### Patrol in Force

An Attacker Stratagem that allows the deployment of an additional unit with the Troops Battlefield Role during deployment, costing Command Points.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Attacker, deployment

**Related:** Patrol

---

#### Encircling Reinforcements

An Attacker Stratagem allowing a unit arriving from Reserve to be set up anywhere within 6 inches of any battlefield edge except the Defender’s, costing Command Points.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Attacker, unit placement

**Related:** Reinforcement Points, Tactical Priority

---

#### Iron Discipline

#### Return Fire

A Defender Stratagem that lets a unit targeted by shooting during the opponent’s first Shooting phase immediately make a shooting attack, costing 2 Command Points.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Defender, special ability

**Related:** Iron Discipline

---

#### The Tables Turned

A Defender Stratagem used immediately after deployment that allows the Defender to roll a dice to potentially gain the first turn on a roll of 6, costing 1 Command Point.

**Tags:** Stratagem, Defender, turn order

#### Gauss weapons

#### Stronghold Assault Scenario

#### Targeting Auger

A defensive weapon system housed in a bunker or fortress that allows the Defender to direct an artillery strike at the start of each shooting phase by placing and moving a marker on the battlefield.

**Tags:** game mechanics, weapon system, defense

**Related:** Adeptus Mechanicus

---

#### Escape Hatch

A Defender stratagem that reduces the chance of garrisoning units being slain upon bunker or fortress destruction, costing 1 Command Point (CP).

**Tags:** stratagem, game mechanics, defender ability

**Related:** Bunker

---

#### Sappers

An Attacker stratagem used before fighting a bunker or fortress that provides a +1 bonus to all wound rolls during that fight phase at a cost of 1 Command Point (CP).

**Tags:** stratagem, game mechanics, attacker ability

**Related:** Bunker

---

#### Critical City Ruins

Specific city ruin objectives that players aim to control for a major victory in Cities of Death scenarios, controlled by having more models on or in the ruin.

#### Underdog

The player whose army has the lower Power Level or, if tied, the one who assigned deployment zones, receiving certain benefits during battle.

**Related:** State of the Imperium

---

#### Fire in the Hole Rule

An advantage rule where grenades re-roll all failed wound rolls and random-attacks always deal maximum attacks when targeting units in ruins.

**Tags:** combat mechanic, grenades, urban warfare

**Related:** State of the Imperium

---

#### Booby Traps Stratagem

A rule to secretly designate a city ruin empty of models to contain hidden traps that cause D3 mortal wounds (D6 if advancing) when enemy units enter it for the first time.

**Also known as:** Booby Traps

**Tags:** stratagem, traps, urban combat

**Related:** Critical City Ruins

---

#### Medicae Facility Stratagem

A rule allowing nomination of a city ruin as a medical facility where models inside have a 1-in-6 chance to heal wounds instead of losing them.

**Also known as:** Medicae Facility

**Tags:** stratagem, healing, urban terrain

**Related:** Critical City Ruins

---

#### Sewer Rats Stratagem

A tactic allowing an infantry unit to start the game infiltrated in the sewers and deploy at street level later more than 9 inches from enemy units and not inside ruins.

**Also known as:** Sewer Rats

**Tags:** stratagem, deployment, urban warfare

---

#### Height Advantage

A combat benefit gained when shooting from upper levels of ruins at targets at least 3 inches below, which ignores target cover bonuses.

**Tags:** combat mechanics, terrain elevation

**Related:** Battlefield Terrain Features

---

#### Ruined Buildings

Crumbling urban structures that provide elevated firing positions, cover, and play a key role in tactical urban battles within Cities of Death scenarios.

**Also known as:** City Ruins

**Tags:** terrain, urban warfare, cover

**Related:** Infantry, Bastion

---

#### Storm and Defend

A victory condition awarding 3 victory points for each objective marker a player controls at game end, determined by having more models within 3 inches of the marker.

Rules used by the Attacker to bring units onto the battlefield during the game rather than deploying them before the game starts.

#### Tenacious Survivor

#### Legendary Fighter

Noble pilots of Imperial Knights—large armoured walkers—who trace bloodlines back to Terra and swear fealty to the Golden Throne or Adeptus Mechanicus; some become Freeblades, fighting independently.

**Also known as:** Glorious Households, Defenders from the Old Night, Imperial Knights

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Imperium, Military, Nobility, Pilots

**Related:** Freeblades, Adeptus Astartes Chapters

---

#### Tithe of Psykers

A levy imposed by the Administratum on planets requiring delivery of a quota of psykers to the Imperium.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Imperium, Taxation, Psionics

**Related:** Imperial Tithe

---

#### Planetary Governors

Local rulers on individual planets responsible for maintaining order, providing troops to the Astra Militarum, enforcing Imperial decrees, and paying tithes to the Administratum.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Imperium, Governance, Military

**Related:** Astra Militarum

---

#### Rogue Traders

Licensed explorers and Emperor’s emissaries authorized to explore uncharted regions of space and exercise full authority to negotiate, bartered or destroy as necessary for the Imperium.

**Also known as:** The hand that draws the map

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Imperium, Exploration, Government Agents

**Related:** The Imperium of Man

---

#### League of Black Ships

One of the two main bodies of the Adeptus Astra Telepathica responsible for the transportation and recruitment of psykers.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Imperium, Organisations, Psionics

**Related:** The Imperium of Man

---

#### Forge Worlds

Planets operated by the Adeptus Mechanicus that manufacture weapons, armor, ships, and war machines for the Imperium.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Imperium, Manufacturing, Planets

**Related:** The Imperium of Man, Emperor’s Golden Throne

#### Emperor’s Golden Throne

An ancient, arcane device preserved by the Adeptus Mechanicus that sustains the Emperor's life and power.

**Related:** Forge Worlds

#### Third Eye

A unique mutant organ possessed by Navigators that grants the ability to perceive and navigate warp space.

**Tags:** Warhammer 40k, Mutations, Navigation, Warp Space

#### Tithes

Resources and contributions collected by the Adeptus Administratum from Imperial worlds to support the Imperium's vast bureaucracy and military.

Individuals or factions within the Imperium who betray Humanity from within, often allying with Chaos or acting against the Imperium's interests.

The current era in Warhammer 40,000, approximately ten thousand years old, marked by myth, ignorance, constant war, and survival as the ultimate victory.

A vast, sprawling human empire in Warhammer 40,000 that spans the galaxy, ruled by a rigid bureaucratic and religious hierarchy, fighting for survival against alien threats and internal traitors.

#### Head swaps

#### Drybrushing

A painting method where a brush with minimal paint is lightly dragged across textured surfaces of a miniature to highlight raised areas.

**Related:** Citadel Paint System

#### Washing

A painting technique that applies a thinned, pigment-rich paint over miniatures to create shadows and enhance details.

**Tags:** painting technique, miniatures, hobby

**Related:** Citadel Paint System
